\n117: // QueryEngine defines the interface for the *promql.Engine, so it can be replaced, wrapped or mocked.\n118: type QueryEngine interface {\n119: \tNewInstantQuery(ctx context.Context, q storage.Queryable, opts QueryOpts, qs string, ts time.Time) (Query, error)\n120: \tNewRangeQuery(ctx context.Context, q storage.Queryable, opts QueryOpts, qs string, start, end time.Time, interval time.Duration) (Query, error)\n121: }\n122: \n123: var _ QueryLogger = (*logging.JSONFileLogger)(nil)\n124: \n125: // QueryLogger is an interface that can be used to log all the queries logged\n126: // by the engine.\n127: type QueryLogger interface {\n128: \tslog.Handler\n129: \tio.Closer\n130: }\n131: \n132: // A Query is derived from a raw query string and can be run against an engine\n133: // it is associated with.\n134: type Query interface {\n135: \t// Exec processes the query. Can only be called once.\n136: \tExec(ctx context.Context) *Result\n137: \t// Close recovers memory used by the query result.\n138: \tClose()\n139: \t// Statement returns the parsed statement of the query.\n140: \tStatement() parser.Statement\n141: \t// Stats returns statistics about the lifetime of the query.\n142: \tStats() *stats.Statistics\n143: \t// Cancel signals that a running query execution should be aborted.\n144: \tCancel()\n145: \t// String returns the original query string.\n146: \tString() string\n147: }\n148: \n149: type PrometheusQueryOpts struct {\n150: \t// Enables recording per-step statistics if the engine has it enabled as well. err != nil {\n252: \t\treturn contextErr(err, env)\n253: \t}\n254: \treturn nil\n255: }\n256: \n257: func contextErr(err error, env string) error {\n258: \tswitch {\n259: \tcase errors.Is(err, context.Canceled):\n260: \t\treturn ErrQueryCanceled(env)\n261: \tcase errors.Is(err, context.DeadlineExceeded):\n262: \t\treturn ErrQueryTimeout(env)\n263: \tdefault:\n264: \t\treturn err\n265: \t}\n266: }\n267: \n268: // QueryTracker provides access to two features:\n269: //\n270: // 1) Tracking of active query. If PromQL engine crashes while executing any query, such query should be present\n271: // in the tracker on restart, hence logged. After the logging on restart, the tracker gets emptied.\n272: //\n273: // 2) Enforcement of the maximum number of concurrent queries.\n274: type QueryTracker interface {\n275: \tio.Closer\n276: \n277: \t// GetMaxConcurrent returns maximum number of concurrent queries that are allowed by this tracker.\n278: \tGetMaxConcurrent() int\n279: \n280: \t// Insert inserts query into query tracker. This call must block if maximum number of queries is already running.\n281: \t// If Insert doesn't return error then returned integer value should be used in subsequent Delete call.\n282: \t// Insert should return error if context is finished before query can proceed, and integer value returned in this case should be ignored by caller.\n283: \tInsert(ctx context.Context, query string) (int, error)\n284: \n285: \t// Delete removes query from activity tracker. InsertIndex is value returned by Insert call.\n286: \tDelete(insertIndex int)\n287: }\n288: \n289: // EngineOpts contains configuration options used when creating a new Engine.\n290: type EngineOpts struct {\n291: \tLogger             *slog.Logger\n292: \tReg                prometheus.Registerer\n293: \tMaxSamples         int\n294: \tTimeout            time.Duration\n295: \tActiveQueryTracker QueryTracker\n296: \t// LookbackDelta determines the time since the last sample after which a time\n297: \t// series is considered stale.\n298: \tLookbackDelta time.Duration\n299: \n300: \t// NoStepSubqueryIntervalFn is the default evaluation interval of\n301: \t// a subquery in milliseconds if no step in range vector was specified `[30m:<step>]`.\n302: \tNoStepSubqueryIntervalFn func(rangeMillis int64) int64\n303: \n304: \t// EnableAtModifier if true enables @ modifier. This\n305: \t// is supposed to be enabled for regular PromQL (as of Prometheus v2.33)\n306: \t// but the option to disable it is still provided here for those using\n307: \t// the Engine outside of Prometheus.\n308: \tEnableAtModifier bool\n309: \n310: \t// EnableNegativeOffset if true enables negative (-) offset\n311: \t// values. Disabled otherwise. This is supposed to be enabled for\n312: \t// regular PromQL (as of Prometheus v2.33) but the option to disable it\n313: \t// is still provided here for those using the Engine outside of\n314: \t// Prometheus.\n315: \tEnableNegativeOffset bool\n316: \n317: \t// EnablePerStepStats if true allows for per-step stats to be computed on request. Disabled otherwise.\n318: \tEnablePerStepStats bool\n319: \n320: \t// EnableDelayedNameRemoval delays the removal of the __name__ label to the last step of the query evaluation.\n321: \t// This is useful in certain scenarios where the __name__ label must be preserved or where applying a\n322: \t// regex-matcher to the __name__ label may otherwise lead to duplicate labelset errors.\n323: \tEnableDelayedNameRemoval bool\n324: \t// EnableTypeAndUnitLabels will allow PromQL Engine to make decisions based on the type and unit labels.\n325: \tEnableTypeAndUnitLabels bool\n326: }\n327: \n328: // Engine handles the lifetime of queries from beginning to end.\n329: // It is connected to a querier.\n330: type Engine struct {\n331: \tlogger                   *slog.Logger\n332: \tmetrics \n454: // SetQueryLogger sets the query logger.\n455: func (ng *Engine) SetQueryLogger(l QueryLogger) {\n456: \tng.queryLoggerLock.Lock()\n457: \tdefer ng.queryLoggerLock.Unlock()\n458: \n459: \tif NewPrometheusQueryOpts(false, 0)\n524: \t}\n525: \n526: \tlookbackDelta := opts.LookbackDelta()\n527: \tif lookbackDelta <= 0 {\n528: \t\tlookbackDelta = ng.lookbackDelta\n529: \t}\n530: \n531: \tes opts.EnablePerStepStats()),\n543: \t\tqueryable:   q,\n544: \t}\n545: \treturn &es.Expr, qry\n546: }\n547: \n548: var (\n549: \tErrValidationAtModifierDisabled     = errors.New(\"@ modifier is disabled\")\n550: \tErrValidationNegativeOffsetDisabled = errors.New(\"negative offset is disabled\")\n551: )\n552: \n553: func (ng *Engine) validateOpts(expr parser.Expr) error {\n554: \tif ng.enableAtModifier && ng.enableNegativeOffset {\n555: \t\treturn nil\n556: \t}\n557: \n558: \tvar atModifierUsed, negativeOffsetUsed bool\n559: \n560: \tvar validationErr error\n561: \tparser.Inspect(expr, func(node parser.Node, _ []parser.Node) error {\n562: \t\tswitch n := node.(type) {\n563: \t\tcase *parser.VectorSelector:\n564: \t\t\tif n.Timestamp != nil || n.StartOrEnd == \t\t}\n597: \n598: \t\treturn nil\n599: \t})\n600: \n601: \treturn validationErr\n602: }\n603: \n604: // NewTestQuery injects special behaviour into Query for testing.\n605: func (ng *Engine) NewTestQuery(f func(context.Context) error) Query {\n606: \tqry := &query{\n607: \t\tq:           \"test statement\",\n608: \t\tstmt:        parser.TestStmt(f),\n609: \t\tng:          ng,\n610: \t\tstats:       stats.NewQueryTimers(),\n611: \t\tsampleStats: stats.NewQuerySamples(ng.enablePerStepStats),\n612: \t}\n613: \treturn qry\n614: }\n615: \n616: // exec executes the query.\n617: //\n618: // At this point per query only one EvalStmt is evaluated. Alert and record\n619: // statements are not handled by the Engine.\n620: func (ng *Engine) exec(ctx context.Context, q *query) (v parser.Value, ws annotations.Annotations, err error) {\n621: \tng.metrics.currentQueries.Inc()\n622: \tdefer func() {\n623: \t\tng.metrics.currentQueries.Dec()\n624: \t\tng.metrics.querySamples.Add(float64(q.sampleStats.TotalSamples))\n625: \t}()\n626: \n627: \tctx, cancel := context.WithTimeout(ctx, ng.timeout)\n628: \tq.cancel = cancel\n629: \n630: \tdefer func() {\n631: \t\tng.queryLoggerLock.RLock()\n632: \t\tif l := ng.queryLogger; l != nil {\n633: \t\t\tlogger := slog.New(l)\n634: \t\t\tf := make([]slog.Attr, 0, 16) // Probably enough up front to not need to reallocate on append.\n635: \n636: \t\t\tparams := make(map[string]any, 4)\n637: \t\t\tparams[\"query\"] = q.q\n638: \t\t\tif eq, ok := q.Statement().(*parser.EvalStmt); ok {\n639: \t\t\t\tparams[\"start\"] = formatDate(eq.Start)\n640: \t\t\t\tparams[\"end\"] = formatDate(eq.End)\n641: \t\t\t\t// The step provided by the user is in seconds.\n642: \t\t\t\tparams[\"step\"] = int64(eq.Interval / (time.Second / time.Nanosecond))\n643: \t\t\t}\n644: \t\t\tf = append(f, slog.Any(\"params\", params))\n645: \t\t\tif err != nil {\n646: \t\t\t\tf = append(f, slog.Any(\"error\", err))\n647: \t\t\t}\n648: \t\t\tf = append(f, slog.Any(\"stats\", stats.NewQueryStats(q.Stats())))\n649: \t\t\tif span := trace.SpanFromContext(ctx); span != nil {\n650: \t\t\t\tf = append(f, slog.Any(\"spanID\", span.SpanContext().SpanID()))\n651: \t\t\t}\n652: \t\t\tif origin := ctx.Value(QueryOrigin{}); origin != nil {\n653: \t\t\t\tfor k, v := range origin.(map[string]any) {\n654: \t\t\t\t\tf = append(f, slog.Any(k, v))\n655: \t\t\t\t}\n656: \t\t\t}\n657: \t\t\tlogger.LogAttrs(context.Background(), slog.LevelInfo, \"promql query logged\", f...)\n658: \t\t\t// TODO: @tjhop -- do we still need this metric/error log if logger doesn't return errors?\n659: \t\t\t// ng.metrics.queryLogFailures.Inc()\n660: \t\t\t// ng.logger.Error(\"can't log query\", \"err\", err)\n661: \t\t}\n662: \t\tng.queryLoggerLock.RUnlock()\n663: \t}()\n664: \n665: \texecSpanTimer, ctx := q.stats.GetSpanTimer(ctx, stats.ExecTotalTime)\n666: \tdefer execSpanTimer.Finish()\n667: \n668: \tfinishQueue, err := ng.queueActive(ctx, q)\n669: \tif err != nil {\n670: \t\treturn nil, nil, err\n671: \t}\n672: \tdefer finishQueue()\n673: \n674: \t// Cancel when execution is done or an error was raised.\n675: \tdefer q.cancel()\n676: \n677: \tevalSpanTimer, ctx := q.stats.GetSpanTimer(ctx, stats.EvalTotalTime)\n678: \tdefer evalSpanTimer.Finish()\n679: \n680: \t// The base context might already be canceled on the first iteration (e.g. during shutdown).\n681: \tif err := contextDone(ctx, env); err != nil {\n682: \t\treturn nil, nil, err\n683: \t}\n684: \n685: \tswitch s := q.Statement().(type) {\n686: \tcase *parser.EvalStmt:\n687: \t\treturn ng.execEvalStmt(ctx, q, s)\n688: \tcase parser.TestStmt:\n689: \t\treturn nil, nil, s(ctx)\n690: \t}\n691: \n692: \tpanic(fmt.Errorf(\"promql.Engine.exec: unhandled statement of type %T\", q.Statement()))\n693: }\n694: \n695: // Log query in active log. The active log guarantees that we don't run over\n696: // MaxConcurrent queries.\n697: func (ng *Engine) queueActive(ctx context.Context, q *query) (func(), error) {\n698: \tif ng.activeQueryTracker == nil {\n699: \t\treturn func() {}, nil\n700: \t}\n701: \tqueueSpanTimer, _ := q.stats.GetSpanTimer(ctx, stats.ExecQueueTime, ng.metrics.queryQueueTime)\n702: \tqueryIndex, err := ng.activeQueryTracker.Insert(ctx, q.q)\n703: \tqueueSpanTimer.Finish()\n704: \treturn func() { ng.activeQueryTracker.Delete(queryIndex) }, err\n705: }\n706: \n707: func timeMilliseconds(t time.Time) int64 {\n708: \treturn t.UnixNano() / int64(time.Millisecond/time.Nanosecond)\n709: }\n710: \n711: func durationMilliseconds(d time.Duration) int64 {\n712: \treturn int64(d / (time.Millisecond / time.Nanosecond))\n713: }\n714: \n715: // execEvalStmt evaluates the expression of an evaluation statement for the given time range.\n716: func (ng *Engine) execEvalStmt(ctx context.Context, query *query, s *parser.EvalStmt) (parser.Value, annotations.Annotations, error) {\n717: \tprepareSpanTimer, ctxPrepare := query.stats.GetSpanTimer(ctx, stats.QueryPreparationTime, ng.metrics.queryPrepareTime)\n718: \tmint, maxt := FindMinMaxTime(s)\n719: \tquerier, err := query.queryable.Querier(mint, maxt)\n720: \tif err != nil {\n721: \t\tprepareSpanTimer.Finish()\n722: \t\treturn nil, nil, err\n723: \t}\n724: \tdefer querier.Close()\n725: \n726: \tng.populateSeries(ctxPrepare, querier, s)\n727: \tprepareSpanTimer.Finish()\n728: \n729: \t// Modify the offset of vector and matrix selectors for the @ modifier\n730: \t// w.r.t. the start time since only 1 evaluation will be done on them.\n731: \tsetOffsetForAtModifier(timeMilliseconds(s.Start), s.Expr)\n732: \tevalSpanTimer, ctxInnerEval := query.stats.GetSpanTimer(ctx, stats.InnerEvalTime, ng.metrics.queryInnerEval)\n733: \t// Instant evaluation. and ranges of all subqueries in the path.\n841: // If the @ modifier is used, then the offset and range is w.r.t. that timestamp\n842: // (i.e. the sum is reset when we have @ modifier).\n843: // The returned *int64 is the closest timestamp that was seen. nil for no @ modifier.\n844: func subqueryTimes(path []parser.Node) (time.Duration, time.Duration, *int64) {\n845: \tvar (\n846: \t\tsubqOffset, subqRange time.Duration\n847: \t\tts                    int64 = math.MaxInt64\n848: \t)\n849: \tfor _, node := range path {\n850: \t\tif n, ok := node.(*parser.SubqueryExpr); ok {\n851: \t\t\tsubqOffset += n.OriginalOffset\n852: \t\t\tsubqRange += n.Range\n853: \t\t\tif n.Timestamp != nil {\n854: \t\t\t\t// The @ modifier on subquery invalidates all the offset and\n855: \t\t\t\t// range till now. Hence resetting it here.\n856: \t\t\t\tsubqOffset = n.OriginalOffset\n857: \t\t\t\tsubqRange = n.Range\n858: \t\t\t\tts = *n.Timestamp\n859: \t\t\t}\n860: \t\t}\n861: \t}\n862: \tvar tsp *int64\n863: \tif ts != math.MaxInt64 {\n864: \t\ttsp = &ts\n865: \t}\n866: \treturn subqOffset, subqRange, tsp\n867: }\n868: \n869: // FindMinMaxTime returns the time in milliseconds of the earliest and latest point in time the statement will try to process.\n870: // This takes into account offsets, @ modifiers, and range selectors.\n871: // If the statement does not select series, then FindMinMaxTime returns (0, 0).\n872: func FindMinMaxTime(s *parser.EvalStmt) (int64, int64) {\n873: \tvar minTimestamp, maxTimestamp int64 = math.MaxInt64, math.MinInt64\n874: \t// Whenever a MatrixSelector is evaluated, evalRange is set to the corresponding range.\n875: \t// The evaluation of the VectorSelector inside then evaluates the given range and unsets\n876: \t// the variable.\n877: \tvar evalRange time.Duration\n878: \tparser.Inspect(s.Expr, func(node parser.Node, path []parser.Node) error {\n879: \t\tswitch n := node.(type) {\n880: \t\tcase *parser.VectorSelector:\n881: \t\t\tstart, end := getTimeRangesForSelector(s, n, path, evalRange)\n882: \t\t\tif start < minTimestamp {\n883: \t\t\t\tminTimestamp = start\n884: \t\t\t}\n885: \t\t\tif end > maxTimestamp {\n886: \t\t\t\tmaxTimestamp = end\n887: \t\t\t}\n888: \t\t\tevalRange = 0\n889: \t\tcase *parser.MatrixSelector:\n890: \t\t\tevalRange = n.Range\n891: \t\t}\n892: \t\treturn nil\n893: \t})\n894: \n895: \tif maxTimestamp == math.MinInt64 {\n896: \t\t// This happens when there was no selector. Hence no time range to select.\n897: \t\tminTimestamp = 0\n898: \t\tmaxTimestamp = 0\n899: \t}\n900: \n901: \treturn minTimestamp, maxTimestamp\n902: }\n903: \n904: func getTimeRangesForSelector(s *parser.EvalStmt, n *parser.VectorSelector, path []parser.Node, evalRange time.Duration) (int64, int64) {\n905: \tstart, end := timestamp.FromTime(s.Start), timestamp.FromTime(s.End)\n906: \tsubqOffset, subqRange, subqTs := subqueryTimes(path)\n907: \n908: \tif subqTs != nil {\n909: \t\t// The timestamp on the subquery overrides the eval statement time ranges.\n910: \t\tstart = *subqTs\n911: \t\tend = *subqTs\n912: \t}\n913: \n914: \tif n.Timestamp != nil {\n915: \t\t// The timestamp on the selector overrides everything.\n916: \t\tstart = *n.Timestamp\n917: \t\tend = *n.Timestamp\n918: \t} else {\n919: \t\toffsetMilliseconds := durationMilliseconds(subqOffset)\n920: \t\tstart = start - offsetMilliseconds - durationMilliseconds(subqRange)\n921: \t\tend -= offsetMilliseconds\n922: \t}\n923: \n924: \tif evalRange == 0 {\n925: \t\t// Reduce the start by one fewer ms than the lookback delta\n926: \t\t// because wo want to exclude samples that are precisely the\n927: \t\t// lookback delta before the eval time.\n928: \t\tstart -= durationMilliseconds(s.LookbackDelta) - 1\n929: \t} else {\n930: \t\t// For all matrix queries we want to ensure that we have\n931: \t\t// (end-start) + range selected this way we have `range` data\n932: \t\t// before the start time. We subtract one from the range to\n933: \t\t// exclude samples positioned directly at the lower boundary of\n934: \t\t// the range.\n935: \t\tstart -= durationMilliseconds(evalRange) - 1\n936: \t}\n937: \n938: \toffsetMilliseconds := durationMilliseconds(n.OriginalOffset)\n939: \tstart -= offsetMilliseconds\n940: \tend -= offsetMilliseconds\n941: \n942: \treturn start, end\n943: }\n944: \n945: func (ng *Engine) getLastSubqueryInterval(path []parser.Node) time.Duration {\n946: \tvar interval time.Duration\n947: \tfor _, node := range path {\n948: \t\tif n, ok := \n1057: type errWithWarnings struct {\n1058: \terr      error\n1059: \twarnings annotations.Annotations\n1060: }\n1061: \n1062: func (e errWithWarnings) Error() string { return e.err.Error() }\n1063: \n1064: // An evaluator evaluates the given expressions over the given fixed\n1065: // timestamps. It is attached to an engine through which it connects to a\n1066: // querier and reports errors. On timeout or cancellation of its context it\n1067: // terminates.\n1068: type evaluator struct {\n1069: \tstartTimestamp int64 // Start time in milliseconds.\n1070: \tendTimestamp   int64 // End time recover(expr parser.Expr, ws *annotations.Annotations, errp *error) {\n1096: \te := recover()\n1097: \tif e == nil {\n1098: \t\treturn\n1099: \t}\n1100: \n1101: \tswitch err := e.(type) {\n1102: \tcase runtime.Error:\n1103: \t\t// Print the stack trace but do not inhibit the running application.\n1104: \t\tbuf := make([]byte, 64<<10)\n1105: \t\tbuf = buf[:runtime.Stack(buf, false)]\n1106: \n1107: \t\tev.logger.Error(\"runtime panic during query evaluation\", \"expr\", expr.String(), \"err\", e, \"stacktrace\", string(buf))\n1108: \t\t*errp = fmt.Errorf(\"unexpected error: %w\", err)\n1109: \tcase errWithWarnings:\n1110: \t\t*errp = err.err\n1111: \t\tws.Merge(err.warnings)\n1112: \tcase error:\n1113: \t\t*errp = err\n1114: \tdefault:\n1115: \t\t*errp = fmt.Errorf(\"%v\", err)\n1116: \t}\n1117: }\n1118: \n1119: func (ev *evaluator) Eval(ctx context.Context, expr parser.Expr) (v parser.Value, ws annotations.Annotations, err error) {\n1120: \tdefer ev.recover(expr, &ws,
